## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Population Ecology
**Analysis**: This task belongs to population ecology, specifically studying the population growth rate as a function of time and current population size. The task can be related to understanding the dynamics of population growth, decline, or stability.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t))
- Exponential growth: N = c0 * exp(c1 * t)
- Power-law growth: N = c0 * t**c1
- Malthusian model: N = c0 * exp(c1 * t) (without carrying capacity)
- Verhulst model: dN/dt = rN * (1 - N/K) (adapting carrying capacity and intrinsic growth rate)
- Linear growth: N = c0 + c1 * t
- Gompertz equation: N = c0 * exp(c1 * exp(c2 * t))
- Harmonic population growth: N = c0 * cos(c1 * t + c2) + c3 (relatively less common pattern)
- Ricker model: dN/dt = rN * exp(c1 * (N - K)) (with a nonlinear carrying capacity term)
- Fox-Berlioz model: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (similar to logistic growth but simpler)
- Polynomial growth: N = c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2
- Semi-log growth: ln(N) = c0 + c1 * t
- Semi-log decline: ln(N) = c0 - c1 * t
- Cybernetic model: dN/dt = c0 * (c1 * N + c2 * (N - K)) (a model with a regulatory mechanism)
- Lotka-Volterra model: dN/dt = rN - a * N * P (with a predator-prey interaction)
- Cobb-Douglas population growth: dN/dt = c0 * N**c1 * (K - N)**c2 (describing a nonlinear growth dynamics)
- Brody model: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (expounded to predict when a population will stabilize)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Bifurcation behavior → S-shaped curve or piecewise functions reflecting tipping points
- Coupling/cross effects → Variable products P*t, P**c1 * t**c2, logistic and exponential functions of both variables
- Growth/decay → exp(c*t), exp(-c*t), power-law c*t**c1
- Damping/amplification → Rational fraction with adjustable asymptote (quadratic, polynomial, sigmoidal), no exponential damping
- Sigmoid growth/decline → Exp(-c*x) in a polynomial, sigmoid or similar function e.g., tanh, logistic, inverse error function
- Cooperative binding → Hill-like equation c0 * P**c1 / (P**c1 + c2), logistic fit through (0, 1)
- Assembly and optimization → Lenke, WEibull or Pearson formula to describe resulting accumulation
- Multiplicity/breakpoints → Different combinations of Rational/Exponential term (including multiple x or t)

**GT:**

**Step 1 – Simplify GT:**  
Let A = 0.1699888096710614, B = 1.0472843670254641, C = 10.210545156320043, D = 0.09709294493863778.  
GT = A*(-1 + P/B)*(1 - P/C)*P + A*(1 - P/C)*P + A*(1 - exp(-D*P))*P  
= A*P * [ (-1+P/B)(1-P/C) + (1-P/C) + 1 - exp(-DP) ]  
= A*P * [ (1-P/C)(P/B) + 1 - exp(-DP) ]  
= A*P * [ P/B - P²/(BC) + 1 - exp(-DP) ]  
= A*P - (A/(BC))*P³ + (A/B)*P² - A*P*exp(-D*P).

Thus GT is a cubic polynomial (terms P, P², P³) minus A*P*exp(-D*P). No logarithmic, sine, or other transcendental terms appear.

Candidate 2: `P*(P**2*c0 + P + c1 + c2*exp(P*c3) + c4*(P*c5 + 1))`

= c0*P³ + (1 + c4*c5)*P² + (c1 + c4)*P + c2*P*exp(c3*P).

This expression contains exactly the required basis set: polynomials up to P³ and a P*exp(constant*P) term. No extra basis functions.

**Step 3 – Match coefficients:**  
We need to satisfy:  
c0 = -A/(B*C)  
1 + c4*c5 = A/B  
c1 + c4 = A  
c2 = -A  
c3 = -D.

Using the numerical GT values: A ≈ 0.169989, B ≈ 1.04728, C ≈ 10.2105, D ≈ 0.097093.  
- c0 = -A/(B*C) ≈ -0.169989 / (10.6936) ≈ -0.0159 (real, valid).  
- c2 = -A ≈ -0.169989 (valid).  
- c3 = -D ≈ -0.097093 (valid).  
- The remaining constants (c1, c4, c5) are free. The equations are:  
  1 + c4*c5 = A/B ≈ 0.1623  →  c4*c5 = -0.8377,  
  c1 + c4 = A ≈ 0.169989.  
We can choose, for example, c4 = 1, then c5 = -0.8377, c1 = -0.8300. All are real numbers.  
Hence an exact match is achieved.

**Step 4 – Domain and constraints:**  
The domain assumes non-negative P. The absolute value relaxation is irrelevant here. Candidate 2 uses no forbidden functions. The free constants can be any real numbers, so matching is valid.

**Conclusion:** Candidate 2 is mathematically equivalent to the ground truth.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.1699888096710614*(-1 + P/1.0472843670254641)*(1 - P/10.210545156320043)*P + 0.1699888096710614*(1 - P/10.210545156320043)*P + 0.1699888096710614*(1 - exp(-0.09709294493863778*P))*P
```

Let me expand this. Let me denote α = 0.16999, β = 1/1.04728 ≈ 0.95486, γ = 1/10.2105 ≈ 0.09794, δ = 0.09709.

**Term 1:** α*(-1 + βP)*(1 - γP)*P = α*(βP - 1)*(1 - γP)*P
= α*P*(βP - 1 - βγP² + γP)
= α*(βP² - P - βγP³ + γP²)
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ)P² - P)

**Term 2:** α*(1 - γP)*P = α*(P - γP²)

**Term 3:** α*(1 - exp(-δP))*P = α*(P - P*exp(-δP))

Combining Terms 1+2+3:
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ)P² - P + P - γP² + P - P*exp(-δP))
= α*(-βγP³ + (β+γ-γ)P² + P - P*exp(-δP))
= α*(-βγP³ + βP² + P - P*exp(-δP))

So GT = α*(-βγP³ + βP² + P - P*exp(-δP))

With numerical values:
- αβγ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.95486 * 0.09794 ≈ 0.01589
- αβ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.95486 ≈ 0.16232
- α ≈ 0.16999
- αδ ≈ 0.16999 * 0.09709 ≈ 0.01651

**GT = c_a*P³ + c_b*P² + c_c*P - c_d*P*exp(-c_e*P)**

where c_a < 0, and the key structural form is: **polynomial in P (cubic) plus P*exp(-δP) term**.

The key basis functions are: P³, P², P, and P*exp(-δP).

Now I need to check which candidates can produce this form. The critical element is the **P*exp(-δP)** term. Candidates using `log`, `sin`, `tan`, or other non-exponential functions cannot match this.

Let me check candidates with `exp`:

- **Candidate 2:** Has `c2*exp(P*c3)` → P*(... + c2*exp(P*c3) + ...) = ... + P*c2*exp(P*c3). This gives P*exp(c3*P). Setting c3 = -δ gives P*exp(-δP). The rest: P*(P²c0 + P + c1 + c4*(Pc5+1)) = P³c0 + P² + Pc1 + c4c5P² + c4P. This gives P³c0 + (1+c4c5)P² + (c1+c4)P + c2*P*exp(c3*P). This has P³, P², P, P*exp terms. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 30:** P³c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*log(Pc3+1) + c4 + c5*exp(Pc6). Has log and exp but no P*exp term (it's c5*exp, not P*exp). Also has a constant c4 and log term. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 33:** P*(Pc0 + Pc1*log(Pc2+1) + Pc3*exp(Pc4) + P + c5*log(Pc2+1)). Has P²c3*exp(Pc4) not P*exp. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 41:** Has exp terms but not multiplied by P in the right way. **NO MATCH**

P*(P²c0 + P + c1 + c2*exp(Pc3) + c4*(Pc5+1))
= P³c0 + P² + Pc1 + Pc2*exp(Pc3) + c4c5P² + c4P
= P³c0 + (1+c4c5)P² + (c1+c4)P + c2*P*exp(c3P)
